<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SkyFeb2013_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-SkyFeb2013-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QatarandSellar_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-QatarandSellar-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></td>

<p><b>The Shard</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup> also referred to as the <b>Shard of Glass</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> <b>Shard London Bridge</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> and formerly <b>London Bridge Tower</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weaver_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weaver-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2010_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2010-15">[14]</a></sup> is a 95-storey <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscraper</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southwark" title="Southwark">Southwark</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, that forms part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a> Quarter development. Standing 309.6 metres (1,016 ft) high, the Shard is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of tallest buildings in the United Kingdom">tallest building in the United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Europe" title="List of tallest buildings in Europe">fourth-tallest building in Europe</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings in the world">105th-tallest building in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> It is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_structures_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of tallest structures in the United Kingdom">second-tallest free-standing structure in the United Kingdom</a>, after the concrete tower at the <a href="/wiki/Emley_Moor_transmitting_station" title="Emley Moor transmitting station">Emley Moor transmitting station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emley_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Emley-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard's construction began in March 2009; it was topped out on 30 March 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shard_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shard-19">[18]</a></sup> and inaugurated on 6 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMJ2012_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMJ2012-20">[19]</a></sup> Practical completion was achieved in November 2012. The tower's privately operated observation deck, <a href="/wiki/The_View_from_the_Shard" title="The View from the Shard">the View from the Shard</a>, was opened to the public on 1 February 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SkyFeb2013_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-SkyFeb2013-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ViewfromTop_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ViewfromTop-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open2013Event_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Open2013Event-22">[21]</a></sup> The glass-clad <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_(geometry)" title="Pyramid (geometry)">pyramidal</a> tower has 72 habitable floors, with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_View_from_The_Shard" title="The View from The Shard">viewing gallery</a> and open-air observation deck on the 72nd floor, at a height of 244.3 metres (802 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> It was designed by the Italian architect <a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a> and replaced <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Towers" title="Southwark Towers">Southwark Towers</a>, a 24-storey office block built on the site in 1975. The Shard was developed by <a href="/wiki/Sellar_Property_Group" title="Sellar Property Group">Sellar Property Group</a> on behalf of LBQ Ltd, and is jointly owned by Sellar Property and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Qatar" title="State of Qatar">State of Qatar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QatarandSellar_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-QatarandSellar-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, London-based entrepreneur Irvine Sellar and his then-partners decided to redevelop the 1970s-era <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Towers" title="Southwark Towers">Southwark Towers</a> following a UK government <a href="/wiki/White_paper" title="White paper">white paper</a> encouraging the development of tall buildings at major transport hubs. Sellar flew to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in the spring of 2000 to meet the Italian architect <a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a> for lunch. According to Sellar, Piano spoke of his contempt for conventional tall buildings during the meal, before flipping over the restaurant's menu and sketching a spire-like sculpture emerging from the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bourke_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bourke-24">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2002, the then-<a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Prescott" title="John Prescott">John Prescott</a>, ordered a planning inquiry after the development plans for the Shard were opposed by the <a href="/wiki/Commission_for_Architecture_and_the_Built_Environment" title="Commission for Architecture and the Built Environment">Commission for Architecture and the Built Environment</a> and several heritage bodies, including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Parks_Foundation" title="Royal Parks Foundation">Royal Parks Foundation</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The inquiry took place in April and May 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weaver_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weaver-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> and on 19 November 2003, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Deputy_Prime_Minister" title="Office of the Deputy Prime Minister">Office of the Deputy Prime Minister</a> announced that planning consent had been approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> The government stated that:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Mr Prescott would only approve skyscrapers of exceptional design. For a building of this size to be acceptable, the quality of its design is critical. He is satisfied that the proposed tower is of the highest architectural quality.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Southwark_Towers,_PwC,_London.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg/220px-Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg/330px-Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg/440px-Southwark_Towers%2C_PwC%2C_London.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Southwark_Towers,_PwC,_London.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Towers" title="Southwark Towers">Southwark Towers</a> office block, which was demolished in 2008 to make way for The Shard</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sellar and his original partners <a href="/wiki/CLS_Holdings" title="CLS Holdings">CLS Holdings</a> plc and CN Ltd (acting for the <a href="/wiki/Simon_Halabi" title="Simon Halabi">Halabi Family Trust</a>) secured an interim funding package of £196 million in September 2006 from the <a href="/wiki/Nationwide_Building_Society" title="Nationwide Building Society">Nationwide Building Society</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kaupthing_Singer_%26_Friedlander" title="Kaupthing Singer &amp; Friedlander">Kaupthing Singer &amp; Friedlander</a>. This enabled them to pay off the costs already incurred and to buy out the Southwark Towers occupational lease from the building's tenants, <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Vacant possession of the site was secured a year later, after PricewaterhouseCoopers completed the relocation of their operations.</p>
<p>In September 2007, preparations for the demolition of Southwark Towers began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> However, later that same month, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession">turbulence in the financial markets</a> reportedly put the Shard's construction in jeopardy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> threatening to render the project an example of the <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper_Index" title="Skyscraper Index">Skyscraper Index</a>.</p>
<p>In November 2007, building contractor <a href="/wiki/Mace_(construction_company)" title="Mace (construction company)">Mace</a> was awarded the contract to build the Shard for a fixed price of no more than £350 million. However, this price increased to almost £435 million in October 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2008, demolition of Southwark Towers was visibly under way,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> and by October, the building had been substantially reduced in height, and was no longer visible on the skyline. The demolition was completed in early 2009, and site preparation began for the construction of the Shard.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late 2007, the gathering uncertainty in the global financial markets sparked concerns about the viability of the Shard. However, in January 2008, Sellar announced that it had secured funding from a consortium of Qatari investors, who had paid £150 million to secure an 80% stake in the project. The consortium included <a href="/wiki/QNB_Group" title="QNB Group">Qatar National Bank</a>, QInvest, Qatari Islamic Bank and the Qatari property developer Barwa Real Estate, as well as Sellar Property. The deal involved a buyout of the Halabi and CLS Holdings stakes, and part of the Sellar Property stake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> The new owners promised to provide the first tranche of finance, allowing construction of the tower to begin. In 2009, the State of Qatar consolidated its ownership of London Bridge Quarter, including the Shard, through the purchase of the private Qatari investors' stakes. London Bridge Quarter is today jointly owned by the State of Qatar and Sellar Property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QatarandSellar_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-QatarandSellar-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="490.1429478458" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Steven_Berkoff_on_the_Shard.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
<source data-bandwidth="76620" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (77 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/Steven_Berkoff_on_the_Shard.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source></audio></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steven_Berkoff_on_the_Shard.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audio description of the building by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Berkoff" title="Steven Berkoff">Steven Berkoff</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="720" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg/220px-ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg/330px-ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg/440px-ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ShardRadiatorFloors.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Internal structure of the Shard's spire and radiator floors, seen from the 72nd-floor observatory</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a>, the project's architect, designed the Shard as a spire-like sculpture emerging from the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bourke_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bourke-24">[23]</a></sup> He was inspired by the railway lines next to the site, the London <a href="/wiki/Spire" title="Spire">spires</a> depicted by the 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a> painter <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mast_(sailing)" title="Mast (sailing)">masts</a> of sailing ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2010_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2010-15">[14]</a></sup> Piano's design met criticism from English Heritage, who claimed the building would be "a shard of glass through the heart of historic London", giving the building its name, the Shard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Piano considered the slender, spire-like form of the tower a positive addition to the London skyline, recalling the church steeples featured in historic engravings of the city, and believed that its presence would be far more delicate than opponents of the project alleged. He proposed a sophisticated use of <a href="/wiki/Glazing_(window)" title="Glazing (window)">glazing</a>, with expressive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fa%C3%A7ades" title="Façades">façades</a> of angled glass panes intended to reflect sunlight and the sky above, so that the appearance of the building will change according to the weather and seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> The building features 11,000 panes of glass, with a total surface area of 56,000 square metres (600,000 sq ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TurnerWebsite_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-TurnerWebsite-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard was designed with energy efficiency in mind. It is fitted with a <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">combined heat and power</a> (CHP) plant, operating on natural gas from the <a href="/wiki/National_Grid_plc" title="National Grid plc">National Grid</a>. Fuel is efficiently converted to electricity and heat is recovered from the engine to provide hot water for the building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the destruction of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>'s <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">World Trade Center</a> (WTC) in the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">terror attacks of 11 September 2001</a>, architects and structural engineers worldwide began re-evaluating the design of tall structures. The Shard's early conceptual designs were among the first in the UK to be amended following the publication of the US <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> (NIST) report into the collapse of the WTC. The building is designed to maintain its stability under very onerous conditions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> with its <a href="/wiki/Prestressed_concrete" title="Prestressed concrete">post-tensioned concrete</a> and composite floors, load-bearing pillars and tapering shape giving it a sway tolerance of 400 millimetres (16 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EandTMag_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-EandTMag-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, The Shard claimed first place at the <a href="/wiki/Emporis" title="Emporis">Emporis</a> Skyscraper Awards, recognising buildings over 100 m (328 ft) completed in the previous twelve months. The Emporis judges hailed the building as "a skyscraper that is recognized immediately and which is already considered London's new emblem".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Layout">Layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="3240" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg/220px-Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg/330px-Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg/440px-Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shard_from_Great_Tower_Street.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Shard pictured from <a href="/wiki/Great_Tower_Street" title="Great Tower Street">Great Tower Street</a> in April 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2009, a mobile crane and a small piling rig arrived on site. In early March 2009, the crane began putting steel beams into the ground, as part of preparations for the core of the building. Full construction began on 16 March 2009. Demolition work on New London Bridge House started in May 2009, as part of the concurrent London Bridge Place project. The first steelwork went into the Shard's piles on 28 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Five cranes were used to build the Shard, with four of them 'jumping' with the tower as it rose. Crane 1 was erected in September 2009 and Crane 2 was erected at the beginning of October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> By 20 October 2009, steel beams began appearing on site, with concrete being poured at the northern part of the site, ready for Crane 3.</p>
<p>By March 2010, the concrete core was rising steadily at about 3 metres (9.8 ft) a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> After a pause in March–April 2010, it continued rising, reaching the 33rd floor in mid-June, almost level with the top of <a href="/wiki/Guy%27s_Hospital" title="Guy's Hospital">Guy's Hospital</a>, which stands at 143 metres (469 ft). On 27 July 2010, the core stopped rising, having reached the 38th floor, and was reconfigured for further construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> By mid-November 2010, the core had reached the 68th floor, with the tower's steel reaching the 40th floor and glass cladding enveloping a third of the building. In late November, the core's height exceeded 235 metres (771 ft), ending <a href="/wiki/One_Canada_Square" title="One Canada Square">One Canada Square</a>'s 18-year reign as Britain's tallest building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard's concrete core topped out at the 72nd floor in early 2011, standing at 245 metres (804 ft). The early part of January 2011 saw the installation of hydraulic screens, which were used to form the concrete floors of the hotel and apartment section of the tower, and rose with the floors up to the 69th floor. On 25 January 2011, the concrete pumps began pouring the first concrete floor at the 41st floor. By the end of February 2011, concrete flooring had risen to the 46th floor, with a new floor being poured on average every week. The cladding of the structure also progressed, mainly on the tower's "backpack".</p>
<p>In February 2011, a <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">Red fox</a> (<i>V. vulpes</i>) was discovered to be living on the partially-completed 72nd floor, having climbed the building site's central stairwell. Nicknamed 'Romeo' by the RSPCA, the animal was rescued and later released back into the wild.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Shard,_Inauguration_Lightshow,_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3456" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg/220px-The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg/330px-The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg/440px-The_Shard%2C_Inauguration_Lightshow%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Shard,_Inauguration_Lightshow,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The inauguration of The Shard on 5 July 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>August 2011 saw steady progress in construction, with cladding enveloping more than half the building's exterior. Pouring of the concrete floors reached the 67th floor, and progression on the tower's cladding reached the 58th floor. By mid-August, the core box had been removed. By 19 September 2011, the tower's steel was approaching the height of the completed core, reaching almost 244 metres (801 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> On 24 September, a final crane – at the time, the tallest ever built in Britain – was erected to install the skyscraper's upper spire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> The spire was pre-fabricated and pre-assembled based upon 3D models, and underwent a "test run" in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a> before being lifted onto the building itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LESspire_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-LESspire-54">[53]</a></sup> By late December 2011, the Shard had become <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_European_Union" title="List of tallest buildings in the European Union">the tallest building in the European Union</a>, superseding the <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank_Tower" title="Commerzbank Tower">Commerzbank Tower</a> in Frankfurt, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GulfTi2012_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-GulfTi2012-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard's steel structure was topped out on 30 March 2012, when its 66-metre (217 ft), 500-tonne spire was winched into place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> The steel structure thus reached a height of 308.5 metres (1,012 ft). The final 516 panes of glass were added shortly after, topping the tower out at its full height of 309.6768 metres (1,016.000 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard was inaugurated on 5 July 2012 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Qatar" title="Prime Minister of Qatar">Prime Minister of Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Jassim_bin_Jaber_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Jassim bin Jaber Al Thani">Hamad bin Jassim bin Jaber Al Thani</a>, in a ceremony attended by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew, Duke of York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open572012_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Open572012-59">[58]</a></sup> The inauguration ceremony featured a <a href="/wiki/Laser" title="Laser">laser</a> light show comprising 12 lasers and 30 <a href="/wiki/Searchlight" title="Searchlight">searchlights</a>, which illuminated the building on the London skyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMJ2012_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-DMJ2012-20">[19]</a></sup> Practical completion of the building was achieved in November 2012.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Height">Height</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Height">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Standing 309.7 metres (1,016 ft) at its highest point, and 308.5 metres (1,012 ft) at the highest point of its steelwork,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shard_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shard-19">[18]</a></sup> the Shard became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_European_Union" title="List of tallest buildings in the European Union">tallest building in the European Union</a> in December 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GulfTi2012_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-GulfTi2012-55">[54]</a></sup> and the tallest completed building in Europe on 30 March 2012. It thus surpassed <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank_Tower" title="Commerzbank Tower">Commerzbank Tower</a>, which, at 259 m (850 ft), was Europe's tallest building between 1997 and 2005. Thereafter, the Shard successively exceeded the heights of three Moscow skyscrapers, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triumph-Palace" title="Triumph-Palace">Triumph-Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naberezhnaya_Tower" title="Naberezhnaya Tower">Naberezhnaya Tower</a>, and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Capitals" title="City of Capitals">City of Capitals</a>, each of which had held the European height record for roughly 2.5 years. However, upon its completion in November 2012, Moscow's 339-metre (1,112 ft) <a href="/wiki/Mercury_City_Tower" title="Mercury City Tower">Mercury City Tower</a> replaced the Shard as the tallest in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CutDown_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-CutDown-61">[60]</a></sup> The Shard may eventually be surpassed as the EU's tallest building by the 323-metre (1,060 ft) <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Plaza" title="Hermitage Plaza">Hermitage Plaza</a> building, which is planned to be completed in <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9fense" title="La Défense">La Défense</a>, Paris, in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard is the second-tallest free-standing structure <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_structures_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of tallest structures in the United Kingdom">in the United Kingdom</a>, after the 330-metre (1,083 ft) concrete transmission tower at <a href="/wiki/Emley_Moor_transmitting_station" title="Emley Moor transmitting station">Emley Moor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emley_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Emley-18">[17]</a></sup> Another planned London skyscraper, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Pinnacle_(London)" title="The Pinnacle (London)">Pinnacle</a>, was originally proposed to rival the height of the Shard, but was reduced to a height of 287.9 metres (945 ft) because of concerns from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Civil Aviation Authority">Civil Aviation Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenants">Tenants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tenants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In February 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> reported that the developers of the Shard were in negotiations to secure the first tenants of the building's 25 floors of office space. In May 2013, the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> reported that only six of The Shard's 72 habitable floors were in use, as a combination of high prices and poor situation discouraged buyers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> At the time, potential tenants included financial restructuring specialists <a href="/wiki/Duff_%26_Phelps" title="Duff &amp; Phelps">Duff &amp; Phelps</a>, private equity firm Hatton Corporation and the <a href="/wiki/South_Hook_LNG_terminal" title="South Hook LNG terminal">South Hook Liquefied Natural Gas Company</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shard's fourth, fifth and sixth floors host the HCA (Hospital Corporations of America), part of London Bridge Hospital. The Shard's 31st, 32nd and 33rd floors host three restaurants: Oblix,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Hutong<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> and Aqua Shard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The building's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shangri-La_Hotel" title="Shangri-La Hotel">Shangri-La Hotel</a>, occupying floors 34–52, was initially expected to open by the end of 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> but its opening was ultimately delayed to 6 May 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> In March 2014, Mathys &amp; Squire became the first law firm to take tenancy in the building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> In May 2014, the Foresight Group, an investment firm, moved its head UK office into the Shard on the 17th floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2013, the Qatari broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network" title="Al Jazeera Media Network">Al Jazeera Media Network</a> announced that it would open a new television studio and newsroom for <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_English" title="Al Jazeera English">Al Jazeera English</a> in the Shard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Al Jazeera moved in on 13 September 2014, and its first live broadcast from the building took place on 10 November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> The facility currently houses all primary operations for Al Jazeera Media Network's channels in London; it is capable of running an entire channel independent from Al Jazeera's other hubs, and is the network's second-biggest hub after its facility in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, Qatar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, further tenants for the Shard were announced, including IO Oil &amp; Gas Consulting, <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Office_Group" title="The Office Group">The Office Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> In May 2015, the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recruitment_consultancy" title="Recruitment consultancy">recruitment consultancy</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Half_International" title="Robert Half International">Robert Half International</a> announced that it would move several branches of its business into the Shard, having purchased 20,000 square feet (1,900 m<sup>2</sup>) of floor space on the tower's tenth floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> In August 2015, the international law firm <a href="/wiki/Greenberg_Traurig" title="Greenberg Traurig">Greenberg Traurig</a> announced that it would open its offices on the eighth floor of the Shard by the end of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2016, global digital marketing agency Jellyfish announced they would be moving into the Shard in May 2016, occupying the 22nd floor. Jellyfish has other offices in Reigate, London, Brighton, Durban, Baltimore and New York.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_exploration.2C_BASE_jumping_and_climbing">Urban exploration, BASE jumping and climbing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban exploration, BASE jumping and climbing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In December 2011, a group of recreational trespassers calling themselves the Place Hackers evaded security and made their way to the top of the Shard building site, climbing one of the tallest cranes in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> They later posted photographs of the London skyline taken from the top of the Shard on the Internet and received wide media attention. One member of the group, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> researcher <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Garrett" title="Bradley Garrett">Bradley Garrett</a>, later revealed to various news outlets that over 20 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_explorer" title="Urban explorer">urban explorers</a> had made their way to the top of the building during its construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> In a 2012 article for <i><a href="/wiki/Domus_(magazine)" title="Domus (magazine)">Domus</a></i> magazine, Garrett wrote that "the conceptual barrier to places in our cities is brought about by a process of engineered exclusion" and that the explorers were "cultivating the creative city that money can't buy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BASE_jumping" title="BASE jumping">BASE jumpers</a> reportedly jumped from The Shard more than a dozen times between 2009 and 2012. Four jumps were reportedly made by <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a> roofer Dan Witchalls, who had filmed one attempt with a <a href="/wiki/Helmet_camera" title="Helmet camera">helmet-mounted camera</a>. The highest jump was said to have been from a height of 850 feet (260 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> In March 2016 another person BASE jumped from The Shard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-base-march-16_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc-base-march-16-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 September 2012, a team of 40 people, including <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew, Duke of York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abseiling" title="Abseiling">abseiled</a> from the tower's 87th floor. This feat was performed to raise money for the <a href="/wiki/Outward_Bound" title="Outward Bound">Outward Bound Trust</a> and the Royal Marines Charitable Trust Fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> In November 2012, the French urban climber <a href="/wiki/Alain_Robert" title="Alain Robert">Alain Robert</a> was spotted in the building by security guards. At the end of the month, the Shard's owners won an <a href="/wiki/Injunction" title="Injunction">injunction</a> to prevent him from entering or climbing the building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 July 2013, six female <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> volunteers climbed the Shard and unfurled a flag in protest against <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_exploration_in_the_Arctic" title="Petroleum exploration in the Arctic">Arctic oil drilling</a> by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace2013_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace2013-91">[90]</a></sup> The women announced they were "experienced climbers", but medical personnel were summoned to the base of the tower nonetheless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace2013_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace2013-91">[90]</a></sup> The Shard's staff closed the tower's observatory and gave the women a safety briefing and other advice during their climb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace2013_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace2013-91">[90]</a></sup> After completing their 16-hour climb, the six women were arrested by police on suspicion of aggravated trespass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace2013_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace2013-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Shard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The Shard appears in the 2012 short film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Snowman_and_The_Snowdog" title="The Snowman and The Snowdog">The Snowman and The Snowdog</a></i> and its tie-in computer game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Shard has a significant role in the 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Bells_of_Saint_John" title="The Bells of Saint John">The Bells of Saint John</a>", as it is the headquarters of the episode's antagonist, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Intelligence" title="Great Intelligence">Great Intelligence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eleventh_Doctor" title="Eleventh Doctor">The Doctor</a> vertically rode a motorbike on the face of the building and through a window to reach the Great Intelligence's headquarters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
